  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d749ac32-deed-49b5-a0a8-349bf17545ec'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer222528109174679976">Today is Leonard Peacock’s birthday. It is also the day he hides a gun in his backpack. Because today is the day he will kill his former best friend, and then himself, with his grandfather’s P-38 pistol.<br/><br/>But first he must say good-bye to the four people who matter most to him: his Humphrey Bogart-obsessed next-door neighbor, Walt; his classmate, Baback, a violin virtuoso; L</span>
  <span id="freeText222528109174679976" style="display:none">Today is Leonard Peacock’s birthday. It is also the day he hides a gun in his backpack. Because today is the day he will kill his former best friend, and then himself, with his grandfather’s P-38 pistol.<br /><br />But first he must say good-bye to the four people who matter most to him: his Humphrey Bogart-obsessed next-door neighbor, Walt; his classmate, Baback, a violin virtuoso; Lauren, the Christian homeschooler he has a crush on; and Herr Silverman, who teaches the high school’s class on the Holocaust. Speaking to each in turn, Leonard slowly reveals his secrets as the hours tick by and the moment of truth approaches.<br /><br />In this riveting look at a day in the life of a disturbed teenage boy, acclaimed author Matthew Quick unflinchingly examines the impossible choices that must be made—and the light in us all that never goes out.</span>

</div>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_576347'><a id="like_count_community_question_576347" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/576347?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">32 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13477676-forgive-me-leonard-peacock">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/37688201-nicholas-gomez"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1575856771i/37688201._UY100_CR24,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/37688201-nicholas-gomez">Nicholas Gomez</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    SPOILER: Yes, the ending is miles away from what the rest of the book sets up. Just from a standpoint of psychology, Leonard Peacock is NOT going to b<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    SPOILER: Yes, the ending is miles away from what the rest of the book sets up. Just from a standpoint of psychology, Leonard Peacock is NOT going to be okay. Regardless of what Matthew Quick might or might not be trying to say, there is so much that Peacock himself is not even aware of (as to why he really wanted to kill Asher) that even if he keeps writing his letters and trying to get better, that's just not the way human behavior works. And for a book that's trying to make a character study about this exact matter, it felt very cheap. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I recommend not to search for much information about the book. You will miss all the surprises. All I knew about the book when I started reading, was <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I recommend not to search for much information about the book. You will miss all the surprises. All I knew about the book when I started reading, was that Leonard Peacock has birthday today and he's gonna kill his best friend and then himself. <br /><br />Anyway this is an awesome book. Easy to read, easy to fall in love with. One of the best books I have ever read in my life. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_425255238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425255238" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425255238?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425255238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2406890282895280906"><blockquote>
  <i>I imagined all of my blood flowing out into the snow and watching it turn a beautiful crimson color as Philadelphians walked by in a great hurry, not even pasuing to admire the beauty of red snow, let alone register the fact that a high school kid was dying right in front of their eyes.</i>
</blockquote><br/>I don't know how helpful this review will be because I read most of the book through a film of tears. Which is an embarrassingly melodramatic statement to make after this book managed to be so dark and sad wit</span>
  <span id="freeText2406890282895280906" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I imagined all of my blood flowing out into the snow and watching it turn a beautiful crimson color as Philadelphians walked by in a great hurry, not even pasuing to admire the beauty of red snow, let alone register the fact that a high school kid was dying right in front of their eyes.</i>
</blockquote><br />I don't know how helpful this review will be because I read most of the book through a film of tears. Which is an embarrassingly melodramatic statement to make after this book managed to be so dark and sad without feeling forced or manipulative like my words. But it's true. <br /><br />Some of my tears were laughter; most of them were sadness. I just... I don't know how to review books like this. I want to string together a list of beautiful, funny or sad quotes from the book when what I'm really saying is: "Just read it. Don't take my word for it. Look, it's there. Go love it." Most of the book's strengths can't be talked about without spoilers and one of the main issues in the story is very much needed; there's not nearly enough books out there about it. But I can't tell you what it is.<br /><br />I'm tempted to say "I wish all books were like this" but that would totally defeat the point of what I'm saying. Because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13477676.Forgive_Me__Leonard_Peacock" title="Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock by Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</a> felt so different to everything else out there and that's partly why I loved it so much. Some of Leonard's problems have been explored in other young adult novels, but none of them do it in quite the same way. I especially liked the creative use of letters Leonard wrote to himself from the future (this makes a lot more sense when you read the book, I swear). But, as with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6763730.Sorta_Like_a_Rock_Star" title="Sorta Like a Rock Star by Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Sorta Like a Rock Star</a>, the real strength lies with the vibrant, full-of-life protagonist himself. He takes center stage and captures your attention for the whole book, dragging you into his life until you find it hard to put down the novel and convince yourself he isn't real.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6763730.Sorta_Like_a_Rock_Star" title="Sorta Like a Rock Star by Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Sorta Like a Rock Star</a> is a darker book than the cover would have you think but it looks like sunshine and rainbows when compared to this. And yet, somehow, Quick manages to make the dark story of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13477676.Forgive_Me__Leonard_Peacock" title="Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock by Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</a> work by mixing in some scenes of humour and, ultimately, hope. I can handle dark and depressing stories just fine, but a light at the end of the tunnel to balance out a story where I care so much about the main character is essential. And in this book, I cared so much I couldn't look away. It's such a sad story-- about how Leonard decided his eighteenth birthday would be his last, and why. Taking his grandfather's P-38 pistol in his backpack, he sets out to kill his former best friend and himself. Over the course of the day, we slowly learn the reasons behind Leonard's decision and are forced to sit on the edge of our seats, hoping one of the people in his life breaks the pattern and stops letting him down.<br /><br />Leonard Peacock has to be one of the loneliest characters I've ever encountered. He's weird. He's confused. Part of him wants to die but most of him just wants to be saved. There's a sad honesty to his voice that makes the story so convincing and that much more effective. I also love books that weave in questions about morality and make the reader stop and think for a while. There's plenty of questions being asked here about life, death, parental responsibility, the way we view others, and religion. The last of which, in my opinion, gives us some of the funniest moments of the whole novel (though perhaps not if you're particularly devout). There is some mockery of the whole "believe or be damned to hell" aspect of religion but, let's be honest, that <i>is</i> hilarious.<br /><br />All I can say now is: read this. But be prepared for sadness. There's a sad tone to the novel that goes beyond the "issues" targeted. And I think the reason is Leonard Peacock. Because the author makes you love him and you just want to hug him and solve his problems, knowing that you can't. That's the only reason I can think of to explain why this book was so sad even in the happier bits. And why I was tearing up even when Leonard said <b>"the world would be a better place if they gave medals to great teachers rather than just soldiers."</b> Jeez, I'm going to cry again if I don't stop talking about this book. So, get out of here. Go READ IT.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2406890282895280906" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_698538236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698538236" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/698538236?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=beta-male">beta-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=glbt">glbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698538236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14879461737493010971">I remember the day when Columbine happened. Of course, there have been school shootings before, and school shooting since, but as a young teen at the time, Columbine was the event that hit home...why? Because the people involved could easily have been me, or my friends. It was so covered by the media, we watched the footage in school, there were counselors, there were added security on my campus, there were a lot of hushed conversations, a lot of adults not knowing how to react, wanting to discu</span>
  <span id="freeText14879461737493010971" style="display:none">I remember the day when Columbine happened. Of course, there have been school shootings before, and school shooting since, but as a young teen at the time, Columbine was the event that hit home...why? Because the people involved could easily have been me, or my friends. It was so covered by the media, we watched the footage in school, there were counselors, there were added security on my campus, there were a lot of hushed conversations, a lot of adults not knowing how to react, wanting to discuss it, but fearing that they'll overstep.<br /><br />This is a hard review for me to write, because I'm not sure how I feel about this book. I can relate to him somewhat. I know a lot of Leonard Peacocks in high school. The bullied, the neglected, the intellectually brilliant, yet unwilling to apply themselves because they don't see the point. I can't say whether any of them ever wanted to kill someone. That's not something you share with others, not if you want to get arrested in a post-Columbine world. I feel like Leonard is a cookie cutter stereotype of the kind who could snap. <b>He's unlikeable, he's downtrodden at times, but he never felt like a real character, much less someone with whom I could ever feel anything less than apathy and disgust</b>.<br /><br />I'm not sure what this book was trying to accomplish. Was it trying to make us sympathize with the main character, to understand his life, his mindset, before he sets out to kill Asher? It did not convince me.<br /><br />Was there simply no point? Maybe it is just the story of a teenager who snapped. Maybe we don't have to like the character. Maybe this book is just a mere insight into the mind of a below-average guy. To make us understand that this potential shooter is just like any other self-absorbed teenager all around the world---albeit one with an automatic and a mission to kill?<br /><br />This book is honest with its portrayal of the main character. I did not like Leonard, and I did not begin to have more developed sympathies towards him until the latter third of the novel. It is narrated through a first-person point of view, largely composed of Leonard's internal dialogue as he goes through his final day, peppered through with flashbacks as he remembers events and people from the past, and some really weird "letters from the future."<br /><br />Leonard is not a likeable character at all. Yes, he has a sad past, but to what extent does that excuse anything? Plenty of us have difficult lives, and have grown up all the stronger for it; I'm not convinced that is a justification for violence. He's got a neglectful, clueless mother, but Leonard has some excellent adult friends and mentors--Herr Silverman was a delight. He is bullied at school...somewhat, and I understand, really.<br /><br />I know what it's like to be bullied. Moving to a new country as a child, having a difficult-to-spell name, learning English, looking like a walking toothpick...those aren't exactly the qualities that made me popular as a child growing up. I sympathize with bullying, I really do, but I think it was brushed over too much in this book to make me feel like it was a major issue that ultimately led to Leonard's decision. The young women in the news who were bullied to such an extent that they killed themselves? That devastated me. And while I cannot judge the effects of bullying on every person's state of mind, because everyone perceives and persists through things differently, the bullying was just not well-portrayed, and largely glossed over within this book.<br /><br />Leonard is more self-absorbed and self-conscious than a typical teenager. He is critical of everyone and everything. He is a hypocrite. I'm not saying that teenagers must be perfect in their actions and their thoughts; it is the nature of development that we go through this stage of intense awareness as we grow up...but the things that goes on within Leonard's mind and his actions doesn't exactly endear me to him.<br /><br />One overwhelming impression you get of Leonard is that he asks questions. All the time. He's like a 3 year old who keeps asking why, why, why?! He routinely ditches class dozens of time to conduct what he calls "practice-adulthood days," when he picks a person, stalks them, and seemingly annoys the hell out of him. Leonard has a weakness for old-fashioned movie starlet types, and during one of his "days," he follows a tragic-looking woman into an alley and stalks her. Then he asks her weird, personal questions, then acts offended when she calls him a pervert.<br /><br />On another day, he comes across another one of his Lauren Bacall types, a home-schooled hard-core Christian missionary girl who is spouting the gospels of Jesus at people who, frankly, don't give a crap. Leonard automatically zeroes in on her, and is determined to win her. Like the pretentious, extremely inquisitive little shit that he is, he zeroes in on her, and figures that <b>since he's paying attention to her, since he's singling her out, she should be grateful to him because she owes him something for his expressed interest</b>. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>She kept looking eagerly at the people coming out of the subway station and wasn’t really paying me much attention anymore, which I thought was weird, since I was the only person who had taken her pamphlet. You’d think she’d concentrate on winning me over, right?<i></i></i>
</blockquote>Naturally, when Lauren doesn't fall for him, he thinks she's an evil femme fatale.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I felt so tricked by Lauren. Being eaten by her was one thing, but introducing me to her boyfriend after she’d led me on—that was entirely unacceptable. She used her femme fatale skills to get me into her church, bait-and-switch style.</i>
</blockquote>He's pretentious, he's entitled. He is a special snowflake. Leonard doesn't think the rules apply to him. It's not just ditching school, it's choosing not to answer the multiple choice questions on a two-part exam because he doesn't feel like it. He argues with teachers for shits and giggles. He shows up to class late. He classifies everyone into categories, he never sees the good in things. Granted, skepticism is part of growing up, but he just has an overwhelming amount of it. The jocks are dumb troglodytes, the smart kids are suck-ups. <b>The world is inferior to Leonard Peacock</b>.<br /><br />The reveal behind what made him want to kill Asher Beal was devastating...but the way it was written, the way it was so tightly pushed away by Leonard's narrative didn't make me sympathize with him that much. Yes, I know it is a deeply serious problem, but there's a possibly deliberate lack of emotion that kept him at a distance from me, and I still didn't end up completely understanding what ultimately made Leonard snap. This book never succeeded in convincing me of anything.<br /><br />Possibly. Maybe. Perhaps. Am I meant to enjoy this book? Am I meant to sympathize with Leonard? Am I supposed to hate him? Maybe that's my problem. I enjoy a book that makes me think, but not a book that makes me second-guess myself that much. There's too many questions in my mind throughout reading this book to make it enjoyable; a book doesn't necessarily have to be fun and light to be enjoyable, but this book lacks the quality that absorbs me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14879461737493010971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1809889747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809889747" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809889747?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809889747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2512137286595451496">Leonard Peacock wants to die. <br/><br/>But before he commits suicide, he wants to kill somebody. Other than himself. His former best friend, Asher, for the harm he has caused him in the past. <br/><br/>Now I don’t want to jinx anything—perhaps I speak too soon, as this is only my second book read by Matthew Quick—but I really do believe that this author is slowly but surely becoming a favourite author of mine.<br/><br/>He just KNOWS how to write a novel. And his imagination has no boundaries. In ‘‘Forgive Me, Leonard Peacoc</span>
  <span id="freeText2512137286595451496" style="display:none">Leonard Peacock wants to die. <br /><br />But before he commits suicide, he wants to kill somebody. Other than himself. His former best friend, Asher, for the harm he has caused him in the past. <br /><br />Now I don’t want to jinx anything—perhaps I speak too soon, as this is only my second book read by Matthew Quick—but I really do believe that this author is slowly but surely becoming a favourite author of mine.<br /><br />He just KNOWS how to write a novel. And his imagination has no boundaries. In ‘‘Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock,’’ he has created not only an authentic, believable teenage boy but also a broken young man who will win your compassion and heart in a single chapter. <br /><br />The truth is, Leonard Peacock does not really want to die. In fact, he clings to life. He hopes someone will give him a reason to stay on this earth. He almost begs them to just give him one reason—just one reason. But he thinks he will never be happy again. <br /><br />What an emotional story. Do NOT think that this is some kind of mystery, suspense novel. Not at all. While there is suspense regarding whether he will pull the trigger or not, this is very much a book dealing with mental health and abuse, so definitely of the psychological sort. <br /><br />Matthew Quick writes so perfectly. This is such an atmospheric book—though melancholic. There are moments when I felt confused, moments when I smiled in a sad way, moments when I smiled in a very heartfelt, genuine manner and moments when I downright couldn’t help but tear up a little. <br /><br />This is not a happy book. And it does not have a clear, closed ending. Many have expressed their disapproval of it. I, for one, was shocked to turn the page and see a blank space staring at me. But I think I know how it ends, deep inside my heart, and sometimes—not always—that enough. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2512137286595451496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1508491861" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508491861" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1508491861?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=knots-in-my-stomach">knots-in-my-stomach</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508491861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1679315057731906637"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842601._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
<i>When the low, heavy sky weighs like a lid <br/>On the groaning spirit, victim of long ennui, <br/>And from the all-encircling horizon <br/>Spreads over us a day gloomier than the night;<br/><br/>When the earth is changed into a humid dungeon, <br/>In which Hope like a bat <br/>Goes beating the walls with her timid wings <br/>And knocking her head against the rotten ceiling;</i> <br/>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>Spleen</i></b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Damn you, Leonard Peacock</b> : you made me remember of who used to be one of my favorite poet when I was a teenager. Ha, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13847.Charles_Baudelaire?from_search=true&search_version=service' rel='nofollow noopener'>Baudelaire</a> with</span>
  <span id="freeText1679315057731906637" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842601._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
<i>When the low, heavy sky weighs like a lid <br>On the groaning spirit, victim of long ennui, <br>And from the all-encircling horizon <br>Spreads over us a day gloomier than the night;<br><br>When the earth is changed into a humid dungeon, <br>In which Hope like a bat <br>Goes beating the walls with her timid wings <br>And knocking her head against the rotten ceiling;</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>Spleen</i></b>
</blockquote><br><b>Damn you, Leonard Peacock</b> : you made me remember of who used to be one of my favorite poet when I was a teenager. Ha, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13847.Charles_Baudelaire?from_search=true&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">Baudelaire</a> with his genius misanthropy, his (often) poor opinion of women and his endless melancholy, always full of irony and cynicism... I would have hated him if I didn't love him so much. Truth is, <b>being close to Leonard felt like that : all hate and contempt and understanding and despair. <br><br>Leonard is no conventional hero, and I can see how his unlikeable traits could create great hate in the readers' heart. Not me, though. How much he made me want to hate him, I never did.</b><br><br><blockquote>
<i>When the rain stretching out its endless train<br>Imitates the bars of a vast prison<br>And a silent horde of loathsome spiders<br>Comes to spin their webs in the depths of our brains,<br><br>All at once the bells leap with rage<br>And hurl a frightful roar at heaven,<br>Even as wandering spirits with no country<br>Burst into a stubborn, whimpering cry.</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>Spleen</i></b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842602._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Let's not shy away from the truth : he is a sexist, conceited human being.</b> But see, this is where I have to explain what I hate in books. I hate when sexism is normalized, accepted, encouraged, even. I hate it with passion. Does that mean that every book has to be rid of characters who think like that? No, I don't think so. <b>There is a definite difference between <i>(1)</i> condoning a behavior by giving readers the impression that sexism is normal, and <i>(2)</i> picturing a fucked up character and how he sees life through his prism</b>. It <i>is</i> definitely different, and here lies the talent of an author : for me, a writer in the first situation lets his story tainted by offensive stereotypes, let it <i>drown</i>. A writer in the second position owns it. He controls it. Frankly? It's obvious that what Leonard thinks is often offensive. I mean - GAH. The guy wants to kill someone and himself for fuck sake! Of course his head isn't the better place to be! I sure didn't expect anything else : <b>despair and hate are more often than not intertwined, unfortunately</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
<i>— And without drums or music, long hearses<br>Pass by slowly in my soul; Hope, vanquished,<br>Weeps, and atrocious, despotic Anguish<br>On my bowed skull plants her black flag.</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>Spleen</i></b>
</blockquote><br>Yet I can't deny that <b>the hate - so much hate - gets hard to stomach at times, especially because it is tainted by so much arrogance</b>. Yet I can't completely dismiss his feelings. Yes, he is judgmental, he assumes many things about his classmates and all the adults in his life. All the time. It gets uncomfortable sometimes and I won't deny it. Yet it seemed real to me, because yes, there are kids like him everywhere. Yes, the moral questions he wonders about constantly are valuable. <b>Are we all monsters? Are we delusional?</b><br><br><blockquote>
<i>I have more memories than if I'd lived a thousand years.<br><br>The desire to end all things<br>A heavy chest of drawers cluttered with balance-sheets,<br>Processes, love-letters, verses, ballads,<br>And heavy locks of hair enveloped in receipts,<br>Hides fewer secrets than my gloomy brain.<br>It is a pyramid, a vast burial vault<br>Which contains more corpses than potter's field.<br>— I am a cemetery abhorred by the moon,<br>In which long worms crawl like remorse<br>And constantly harass my dearest dead.<br>I am an old boudoir full of withered roses,<br>Where lies a whole litter of old-fashioned dresses,<br>Where the plaintive pastels and the pale Bouchers,<br>Alone, breathe in the fragrance from an opened phial.</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>Spleen</i></b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842603._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But don't get fooled by his conceited mind. <b><u>Leonard suffers</u>, and at no moment can you dismiss his despair because of his behavior</b>. I couldn't, anyway. Along the way you realize more and more and <i>more</i> that Leonard has problems. <b>Real</b> ones. <b>Devastating</b> ones.<br><br>I know how stupid that can seem because DUH look at what he planned! but <b>seeing him mixing half truths, real despair and delusions - it broke me a little</b>. We have a word in French, <i>le désenchantement</i>. It was often used to refer to the post-1830 generation when youngs didn't know what to do anymore, now that epic careers weren't possible - no more Napoleon - and that the politic system just looked <i>stuck</i>, between Monarchy, Republic and Empire. One of my favorite book of all times, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2067862.Stello" title="Stello by Alfred de Vigny" rel="nofollow noopener">Stello</a>, explores this melancholy through the life of a poet who tries to find what political system would give him the more freedom. Truth is - there's none. Freedom is in him, in his poetic quality, in his <i>otherness</i> - Leonard reminded me of him. It's scary how misunderstanding can lead to violence. <br><br><b>If Leonard wants people around him to be helpless and pathetic, it's only because he <i>is</i>.</b> He made me laugh, though (what? I do have a soft spot for smartasses^^) <s>The Jesus parts were PRICELESS</s><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842604._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
<i>That winged voyager, how weak and gauche he is,<br>So beautiful before, now comic and ugly!<br>One man worries his beak with a stubby clay pipe;<br>Another limps, mimics the cripple who once flew!<br><br>The poet resembles this prince of cloud and sky<br>Who frequents the tempest and laughs at the bowman;<br>When exiled on the earth, the butt of hoots and jeers,<br>His giant wings prevent him from walking.</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>The Albatros</i></b>
</blockquote><br>I can't deny that some parts made me feel so much. Shivering. Tearing up. Yet it wavered - not my interest, because I was hooked from the beginning (and the writing is beautiful) - but the emotion. It was so weird to see that I could connect on such a strong level with Leonard and then just - <i>stop</i>. Perhaps it was meant to be. Perhaps I was way too exhausted. Regardless of the reason, it prevented me from completely love Leonard's story, but didn't hide to me how important this story is. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842605._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's talk about Leonard's relations with women, okay? <b>They made me furious at times</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
<i>A lightning flash... then night! Fleeting beauty<br>By whose glance I was suddenly reborn,<br>Will I see you no more before eternity?<br><br>Elsewhere, far, far from here! too late! never perhaps!<br>For I know not where you fled, you know not where I go,<br>O you whom I would have loved, O you who knew it!</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>To a Passer-by</i></b>
</blockquote><br>Sigh. As other reviewers pointed it, Leonard shares a very bad opinion of women in general and doesn't show any respect most of the time. Plus, he's a stalker. I hated him for it, but as I said earlier, I'm not supposed to love him. I don't have to condone his actions and his way of thinking, and at no moment did I feel any pressure to do so. In my opinion, Quick never intends to redeem him, and I'm okay with that. <br><br><blockquote>
<i>My poor Muse, alas! what ails you today? <br>Your hollow eyes are full of nocturnal visions; <br>I see in turn reflected on your face <br>Horror and madness, cold and taciturn.</i> <br>- <b>Charles Baudelaire, <i>The Sick Muse</i></b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453559141i/17842606._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Truth be told, I'm not sure that this review will help you determine if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13477676.Forgive_Me__Leonard_Peacock" title="Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock by Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</a> is for you. What can I say? I'm not even sure it was for me. What you need to know is that it's by no means a perfect book, with several characters a little too one-dimensional and stereotypical (the mother, for example) and a male lead you'll perhaps want to strangle sometimes. <b>Yet I don't regret reading it, and his story will probably haunt me a long time. I'd say that it means something, doesn't it?</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"First they ignore you, then<br>they laugh at you, then they<br>fight you, then you win."</b>
</blockquote><br><b>PS.</b> All the poems are from William Aggeler's translations (1954), but I strongly advise you to read them in French if you can. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="1679315057731906637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2297534776" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2297534776?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2297534776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7428531012634019174">tw: antisemitism/nazis, suicidal thoughts and actions, depression, rape/sexual assault<br/><br/>It's strange how this book made me feel simultaneously uncomfortable yet touched. Leonard Peacock is purposefully an unlikable character, yet as his mental illness and traumatic past is slowly unveiled, you can't help but root for him and his recovery. This book nearly tore my heart in half just because of how conflicted I was, but I think that was the point. I adored the side characters in this book, and I lov</span>
  <span id="freeText7428531012634019174" style="display:none">tw: antisemitism/nazis, suicidal thoughts and actions, depression, rape/sexual assault<br /><br />It's strange how this book made me feel simultaneously uncomfortable yet touched. Leonard Peacock is purposefully an unlikable character, yet as his mental illness and traumatic past is slowly unveiled, you can't help but root for him and his recovery. This book nearly tore my heart in half just because of how conflicted I was, but I think that was the point. I adored the side characters in this book, and I loved Leonard's narration itself. I was definitely crying at the book's climax. The storytelling is jarring but honest, and I couldn't put this down. <br /><br />My only real critique is that the ending was too abrupt. I feel like it needed one more chapter or an epilogue for some finality, or at least an indication of what the characters ended up doing after the climax of the book. I feel like I still don't quite know if the book ended on a positive or negative note. Was that the intention? <br /><br />Regardless, i'm still wiping mascara smudges off my cheeks from this book. I anticipate I'll be thinking about it for some time, wondering what the characters are up to after the ending of the novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7428531012634019174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1093907720">

<div id="review_1323680313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1323680313" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1323680313?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1323680313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5695155994009157768">I can definitely see why <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13477676.Forgive_Me__Leonard_Peacock' title='Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock by Matthew Quick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</a> is such a beloved book. I believe many readers will find this novel beautiful and heart-breaking; and I did too, to a certain extent. <b>Though I appreciated many things within this book and even found myself emotionally attached to the main character, there were also quite a few elements that really bothered and hindered me at truly loving this story.</b><br/><br/>The story centres around Leonard Peacock who has decided that he is going to kill himself on his</span>
  <span id="freeText5695155994009157768" style="display:none">I can definitely see why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13477676.Forgive_Me__Leonard_Peacock" title="Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock by Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</a> is such a beloved book. I believe many readers will find this novel beautiful and heart-breaking; and I did too, to a certain extent. <b>Though I appreciated many things within this book and even found myself emotionally attached to the main character, there were also quite a few elements that really bothered and hindered me at truly loving this story.</b><br /><br />The story centres around Leonard Peacock who has decided that he is going to kill himself on his eighteenth birthday. On that morning he packs his grandfather’s Nazi gun into his backpack and sets out to kill not only himself, but also his classmate and nemesis Asher Beal. The story follows him throughout the day, as we slowly learn the reasons behind Leonard’s desperation.<br /><br />Leonard’s story and his voice appear <b>very honest and raw</b>. Some of the issues that are targeted are rare in fiction and very much needed (I can’t tell you what it is without spoiling). <b>The book has many strong points; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1251730.Matthew_Quick" title="Matthew Quick" rel="nofollow noopener">Matthew Quick</a> manages to make situations simultaneously depressing and humorous and the novel asks important questions about morality, responsibility and faith.</b> It is also a very engaging story that you will fly through, wanting to know how it ends.<br /><br /><b>And yet, despite all these positive aspects, this book bothered me.</b><br /><br />My main problem was with the protagonist, Leonard Peacock, himself. <br /><br />He is lonely, an outcast, feels out of place. Something devastating happened to him years ago and he didn’t receive any help. He is neglected. I feel horrible for saying this, but although I did feel for Leonard and could relate to him somewhat, I could not make myself root for him all the way. <b>Leonard Peacock is a stereotype for the suicidal teenager.</b> Bullied and misunderstood, very bright but unwilling to apply himself in school. <br /><br />However, this wasn’t even the reason I struggled with him. <b>I disliked him because he was so damn condescending and self-absorbed.</b> Seriously, Leonard believes himself to be a special snowflake, superior to everyone else. In his eyes he can do no wrong. If someone disagrees with him, he immediately discredits them. <b>I understand that he’s had a hard life and is sceptical, but that doesn’t justify the way he treats the people around him.</b> He classifies everything and everyone and doesn’t believe a person could ever truly have good intentions. He also completely disregards rules; in tests he chooses not to answer multiple-choice questions because those are beneath him. What’s the point in doing something you don’t feel like doing?<br /><br />I’m aware that this might have been the point. Leonard is jaded and that is why he sees the world in this light. I don’t want to undermine the truly horrible things that happened to him, his depression is understandable. <b>But I still couldn’t get myself to like him.</b><br /><br />Matthew Quick wants to give us the impression that Leonard is brilliant and mature beyond his years. One of the examples he uses is a question raised by Leonard’s teacher, Herr Silverman. Herr Silverman asks the class what they believe they would have done had they lived during the Second World War in Nazi Germany. Would they have followed or defied Hitler? Leonard answers this question (in his head) honestly with: “I don’t know.” All the other kids in the class however, claim that they would have stood up to Hitler, gone against his ideals etc. Now I don’t know about you, but if a teacher would have asked my old high school class this question, I can guarantee that all of us would have answered the way Leonard did. Which leads to the question: <b>Is Leonard truly that smart and mature, or were the other students just portrayed as particularly ignorant to make him look better?</b><br /><br /><b>I also wasn’t very happy with how Leonard treated women.</b> He meets a girl called Lauren at the train station who is passing out pamphlets on Christianity. He finds her attractive and is immediately infatuated with her. Since he is the only person who took her pamphlet and actually bothered to talk to her, he somehow believes that he “deserves” her. When he finds out she has a boyfriend he gets angry. <br /><br />Leonard also implies that the female teachers are all flirting with the male students. When the school counsellor checks up on him, he believes she is actually flirting with him, when really, she says nothing that would justify this claim.<br /><br />The side characters fell flat for me. <b>They all seemed very stereotypical.</b> Herr Silverman, the perfect teacher. Lauren, the unwaveringly devout Christian. Linda, the totally careless and absent mother. They were all characters I have seen before.<br /><br /><b>Although this review is quite negative, <i>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</i> really isn’t a bad book. I enjoyed it and would recommend it (especially seeing how much everyone else seems to love it); however, I was somewhat disappointed.</b> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5695155994009157768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1983538180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1983538180" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1983538180?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781472209153" href="/book/show/18005172-forgive-me-leonard-peacock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trauma-abuse-recovery">trauma-abuse-recovery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-buylist">x-buylist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=this-shit-made-me-cry">this-shit-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1983538180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10873097532731967716">Books, to me, should not be about moralizing. They should be <i>explorations</i> of controversial ideas and of the horrible things that people can do. And that is exactly what this book is: <b><i>Forgive Me Leonard Peacock</i> avoids moralizing, but also doesn't shy away from the harsh reality of what Leonard plans to do</b>. <br/><br/>And all this is to say that I have seen so many people say that they hate everyone who enjoyed this book. Notwithstanding the fact that I kind of despise that statement, inherently, I completel</span>
  <span id="freeText10873097532731967716" style="display:none">Books, to me, should not be about moralizing. They should be <i>explorations</i> of controversial ideas and of the horrible things that people can do. And that is exactly what this book is: <b><i>Forgive Me Leonard Peacock</i> avoids moralizing, but also doesn't shy away from the harsh reality of what Leonard plans to do</b>. <br /><br />And all this is to say that I have seen so many people say that they hate everyone who enjoyed this book. Notwithstanding the fact that I kind of despise that statement, inherently, I completely disagree. <br /><br />There's so much homophobia here. There's so much misogyny. How dare you excuse it. Here's the thing: this book doesn't excuse <i>any</i> of it. Despite several things I'd usually DNF for— the misogyny and homophobia of the protagonist, namely— this convinced me. How? <b>By narratively showing that all of those things are negative, rather than some accepted behavior.</b> <br /><br />And none of this is to diss the idea that this book goes to far, or doesn't explore Leonard's issues enough. You know what? In terms of the misogyny, I have to agree. I wanted quite a bit more out of Lauren's character; her lack of agency within the narrative is a blatant weak spot. If a stronger character had been given to her, the scenes in which Leonard ignored consent in his interactions with her would've felt like far more of a purposeful decision. <br /><br />This is as many-layered a book as you can get, but first and foremost, it is a character study of a deeply traumatized teenager. And it's a very, very good one. Leonard Peacock has one of the most distinctive voices and personalities I've ever seen in YA. Even though he does a lot of crap wrong - a lot, a lot of crap - I <i>adored</i> his character. The writing is lovely, with a quality that brings you straight into Leonard's mind. His thoughts about the world almost reminded me of <i>A Catcher in the Rye</i> in their matter-of-fact quality. <br /><br />Basically, <b>
  <u>I have met my match in book form.</u>
</b> I read this entire book - yes, the <i>whole damn thing</i> - in an hour and a half without ever breaking, not even to use the bathroom. I don't even think I looked up. I definitely didn't look at the clock. I spent the last 100 pages shaking and feeling as if I couldn't come up for air. This is a book I will not forget for a long, long time, and one I cannot recommend enough.<br /><br />Trigger warnings: rape and sexual assault.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10873097532731967716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_648080618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648080618" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648080618?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=littlebrown">littlebrown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-really-enjoyed-it">i-really-enjoyed-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648080618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12755436999299804752">Recently, I've been reading really depressing books that have both horrified and fascinated me. But out of all of them, <em>Charm and Strange</em> and now <em>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</em> takes the cake for tackling tough, taboo issues. In this case, suicide. Now, the last suicide book I've read was <em>Thirteen Reasons Why</em> and this book can easily be compared to that. But instead of the story being told from tapes from the deceased and another MC, <em>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</em> is told play-by-play from Leonard him</span>
  <span id="freeText12755436999299804752" style="display:none">Recently, I've been reading really depressing books that have both horrified and fascinated me. But out of all of them, <em>Charm and Strange</em> and now <em>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</em> takes the cake for tackling tough, taboo issues. In this case, suicide. Now, the last suicide book I've read was <em>Thirteen Reasons Why</em> and this book can easily be compared to that. But instead of the story being told from tapes from the deceased and another MC, <em>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</em> is told play-by-play from Leonard himself. His voice is real, broken, hurt, confused and relatable. He wants to be seen, remembered. He wants people to acknowledge his existence. So on his 18th birthday he takes his grandfather's war gun trophy and sets out to kill his former best friend and himself.<br /><br />When we are introduced to Leonard, he immediately fills the reader in on his plans, though the ultimate reason why is revealed along the course of his day as he gives away personal items or gifts to four people he regularly interacts with. While Leonard calls them friends, we find that this doesn't accurately describe those relationships. Two mostly tolerate or accept his presence in their routine, but unlike most of his peers, they communicate with him in some way despite being weirded out by his differences. Leonard is vastly different from his classmates and that is quickly apparent in his reasonings and speech. He sees the world and challenges things normal teenagers wouldn't think about. This doesn't do Leonard any favors regarding his popularity, but he brushes this off as ignorance on their part.<br /><br />The thing about Leonard is that he's such a smart character, but he never comes across as pretentious like some characters from other equally morbid novels. (This is me giving <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em> the stink eye.) It's easy to see why he's misunderstood and underestimated, but such a shame to read about such a lonely kid. His situation depressed me on a serious level and I just wanted to give this guy hug. He doesn't have friends his age or even the support of his family. His mother spends her days in New York, living her dream working as a designer and his father is nowhere to be seen, leaving Leonard to mostly fend for himself. Thankfully, Leonard is not entirely alone and when the climax hits, he does begin to see there are people who care about him.<br /><br />If there is one piece of criticism I do have it was the way the Letters From the Future were introduce. In certain chapters of the book, the narrative and setting switches and their isn't any notice. I'll admit to be completely caught off guard to this and confused as to how it held any relevance to the story until after his teacher mentioned them in class. Leonard also has moments when he references footnotes in his narration, which is generally not a style that I love since it causes me to flip back and forth from the footnotes to the story. Word to the wise, reading this one on your kindle might be a royal pain in the ass.<br /><br />All in all, I'm really glad I decided to check <em>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</em> out. It's a very different story, the kind I'm not used to reading. But just like <em>Thirteen Reasons Why</em> and<em> Charm and Strange</em>, it's one I'll probably be thinking about for a while. Highly recommended.<br /><br /><br /><em>ARC was provided by the publisher for an honest review. Thank you!</em><br /><br />More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12755436999299804752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1888894381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1888894381" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1888894381?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316221351" href="/book/show/18774013-forgive-me-leonard-peacock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=psycho">psycho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reality-bites">reality-bites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1888894381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16618085091945491383"><br/><b>3.5 stars </b><br/><br/>This is the one book that perfectly qualifies the funny and heartbreaking description. It’s sad but the depressed really do have a great sense of humor. Until I’ve read the very first page of the book, I honestly thought Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock is mainly a humorous contemporary fiction and I picked it up because I was looking forward to reading something light and funny. It was funny but I was in a complete surprise to find out that it’s a book mainly about depression and suicide a</span>
  <span id="freeText16618085091945491383" style="display:none"><br /><b>3.5 stars </b><br /><br />This is the one book that perfectly qualifies the funny and heartbreaking description. It’s sad but the depressed really do have a great sense of humor. Until I’ve read the very first page of the book, I honestly thought Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock is mainly a humorous contemporary fiction and I picked it up because I was looking forward to reading something light and funny. It was funny but I was in a complete surprise to find out that it’s a book mainly about depression and suicide and yet one that I would recommend over other books that also talk of the same subject matters. <br /><br />Reading the story in the main character’s POV, I appreciate all of Leonard’s very insightful thoughts on humanity and about his waning confidence in people’s ability to be human. I couldn’t blame him because a lot of his thoughts are true. So many people are too busy to care, too busy trying to conform to social norms and all and too busy to be different. It was kind of eerie because we do share a lot of similar thoughts especially dark, twisted ones. Let me just share one:<br /><br />“Whenever I replay this memory, I see myself running, and before I know it I’ve left my spot and I’m a flying cross-check. In my mind, my hockey stick turns into a samurai sword and I decapitate Asher with an awesome swipe so that his head flies through the basketball net.” <br /><br />I don’t always agree with his thoughts though and I even think that some of them are very wrong but he is right when he says, <br /><br />“THINK FOR YOURSELF AND DO WHAT’S RIGHT FOR YOU, BUT LET OTHERS DO THE SAME.” <br /><br />I’m not at all very happy that the story abruptly ended that way but I think the story in general contains really hopeful and powerful messages that everyone will be able to relate to. Plus, I really enjoyed the writing technique. The postscripts and the letters from the future certainly made the entire book unique and creative. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2121641075" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121641075" />
    <a title="Sr3yas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas"><img alt="Sr3yas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520526764p2/23097409.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121641075?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sr3yas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sr3yas" href="/user/show/23097409-sr3yas">Sr3yas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18324127-forgive-me-leonard-peacock">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121641075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4648032891290710277"><b>Forgive me Mathew Quick,</b> because I didn't find your story compelling for most of the part. <br/><br/><b>Synopsis?</b> Leonard Peacock has a shitty life. He is a fictional embodiment of all things that could go wrong with an average 21st-century teenager, bar the drugs. Leonard has no father, no friends of his age, and no girlfriend. What he does have is money, a Mother who doesn't care about him, a <i>Holden Caulfield</i> attitude and a P 38 gun.<br/><br/>And today is his birthday. And the plan? <u>
  <i>He is going to kill his ex-bes</i></u></span>
  <span id="freeText4648032891290710277" style="display:none"><b>Forgive me Mathew Quick,</b> because I didn't find your story compelling for most of the part. <br><br><b>Synopsis?</b> Leonard Peacock has a shitty life. He is a fictional embodiment of all things that could go wrong with an average 21st-century teenager, bar the drugs. Leonard has no father, no friends of his age, and no girlfriend. What he does have is money, a Mother who doesn't care about him, a <i>Holden Caulfield</i> attitude and a P 38 gun.<br><br>And today is his birthday. And the plan? <u>
  <i>He is going to kill his ex-best friend and himself.</i>
</u><br><br>The book is written like <i>The Catcher in the Rye,</i> where the main character talks about his feelings, paints his opinions and narrate his actions until the end of the book. The only way you could probably like the book is if you connect with the character or <b>feel empathy</b> towards him. This differs to person to person, and right now I am standing at <i>"Nah, I am not buying it"</i> side.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484977899ra/21772767.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To Quick's credit, there are some unique characters in this story. One of them is a religious teenage girl and another is a music wizard classmate. The usual characters are also present, like the good guy teacher, old and loving neighbor, and the bully. <br><br>But the character who actually matters is Leonard Peacock as we will be spending <b>entire book inside his head,</b> and unfortunately, he is not very compelling. His monologues are repetitive, his opinions lack originality and it all feels like been there, done that. His lines on how he has a p38 and how he holds power over everyone quickly loses its novelty because of the innumerable repetition of the same dialogue.<br><br>I understand what Quick was trying to convey to readers is important, but the subtle delivery of ideas and all the redundant storytelling style makes it less effective. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505732422i/23954559._SX540_.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b><i>“I’m going to kill you later today,” </i>I say to that guy in the mirror, and he just smiles back at me like he can’t wait.<br><i>“Promise?”</i> I hear someone say, which freaks me out, because my lips didn’t move.<br>I mean—it wasn’t me who said, <i>“Promise?”</i><br>It’s like there’s a voice trapped inside the glass.<br>So I stop looking in the mirror.<br>Just for good measure, I smash that mirror with a coffee mug, because I don’t want the mirror me to speak ever again.<br></b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505732422ra/23954560.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Geez, I thought I had issues!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4648032891290710277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
