    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_655684308" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655684308" />
    <a title="Scarlet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet"><img alt="Scarlet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556098025p2/3839903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655684308?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scarlet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scarlet" href="/user/show/3839903-scarlet">Scarlet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18324127-forgive-me-leonard-peacock">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=whats-the-fuss-about">whats-the-fuss-about</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3839903-scarlet?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655684308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3995060548394026976">Either this book failed to do what it set out to do, or I went in with the wrong expectations. Whatever the case, <i>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</i> did not have any appreciable impact on me.<br/><br/>You see, I read this book hoping to gain some insight into the mind of a school shooter. Someone like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80660.We_Need_to_Talk_About_Kevin?ac=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kevin Khatchadourian</a>, just not so inherently evil. I wanted this book to scare me, stun me, make me question, make me think, maybe break my heart a little. <br/><br/>What I did not want this book to do (and what it essential</span>
  <span id="freeText3995060548394026976" style="display:none">Either this book failed to do what it set out to do, or I went in with the wrong expectations. Whatever the case, <i>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</i> did not have any appreciable impact on me.<br /><br />You see, I read this book hoping to gain some insight into the mind of a school shooter. Someone like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80660.We_Need_to_Talk_About_Kevin?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kevin Khatchadourian</a>, just not so inherently evil. I wanted this book to scare me, stun me, make me question, make me think, maybe break my heart a little. <br /><br />What I did not want this book to do (and what it essentially did) was <b>give me a long list of excuses for why this guy was walking around with a gun in his bag.</b><br /><br />Now, I'm not trying to undermine the gravity of the situation here. Leonard has had a tough life; has endured some horrible things. He's depressed and lonely, he's been bullied, and I understand how difficult that is to get through. But isn't that true for a lot of teenagers?? Not everyone lugs a P-38 to school though. Shouldn't there be something more? Something in the way Leonard's mind works? Something to do with the person that Leonard is rather than the circumstances?<br /><br />The narrative is designed to make you feel sorry for Leonard. I'm afraid that had quite the opposite effect on me - <b>my empathy meter was stuck at zero</b>. This is going to sound highly insensitive but I felt like Leonard was constantly appealing to the sensitive side of me - <i>See how intelligent I am but nobody appreciates me? See how nice a person I am but nobody talks to me? See how profound my questions are but nobody gives a damn? See how none of my friends, and not even my mother, remember my birthday? Doesn't my life suck? Don't you feel sorry for me? Don't you? Don't you?</i> - and all I could do was watch impassively, with the occasional annoyed eye-roll.<br /><br />There are only a handful of characters other than Leonard, but I cannot tell you anything remarkable about them except that <b>they all seem a little extreme</b>. As much as I hope teachers like Herr Silverman exist, he is almost too good to be true. Leonard's mother is way too absent; she has pretty much abandoned her only son and never bothers to return his messages. Asher Beal is... horrible, supposed to be hated. The whats-her-name that Leonard has a crush on is a little too obsessed with Christianity. <br /><br />Leonard himself never became a real person in my eyes. At the best of times, he was nothing more than a string of adjectives, too different and too disjoint to go together. <br /><br />Quick's writing is okay but <b>the structure of the book impedes the flow</b>. The footnotes are more like foot<i>essays</i> - long, meandering recollections that make you forget you're reading a footnote until you're suddenly pulled back to the main narrative, following which it becomes necessary to re-read a few lines to grasp the context again. Then there are these "<i>Letters from the Future</i>" that, looking back, are probably some of the most poignant moments the book has to offer, but because Quick doesn't bother explaining their importance until it's too late, you read them only with a growing sense of bewilderment, wondering why you're suddenly in the middle of a post-apocalyptic water-world.<br /><br />The only point where I felt some semblance of an emotional connection was the very last chapter. It's nothing remarkable, but there is this desperation there that really hit me. It was when I wondered if I had it all wrong. Maybe Leonard was never the "shooter" but just another depressed teenager who, tired of fighting the world, had come dangerously close to giving up altogether.<br /><br />I don't know if I would recommend this book. All my friends who've read it have either given it full-on 5 or a measly 2. <b>If you can empathize with Leonard then maybe you'll love it. I couldn't, so I didn't.</b><br /><br />Forgive Me, Matthew Quick. I'm not impressed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3995060548394026976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_641656155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/641656155" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/641656155?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer641656155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9095726196378294041">Wow what a sad story this was! Told in the voice of a morose, yet incredibly intelligent teenage boy, we're given a raw look into the road to suicide, and how depression affects your thoughts. <br/><br/>What I noticed immediately was the writing style which stood out to me as something very… honest. Not only is it told in first person - which I consider a requirement for a story such as this - but we get a format that emphasizes his unhealthy state of mind even more so. This includes foot notes on his int</span>
  <span id="freeText9095726196378294041" style="display:none">Wow what a sad story this was! Told in the voice of a morose, yet incredibly intelligent teenage boy, we're given a raw look into the road to suicide, and how depression affects your thoughts. <br><br>What I noticed immediately was the writing style which stood out to me as something very… honest. Not only is it told in first person - which I consider a requirement for a story such as this - but we get a format that emphasizes his unhealthy state of mind even more so. This includes foot notes on his interpretations of certain situations and people; pages that only include 1 single word for a whole sentence; "Letters from the future" which had me baffled at first but ended up leaving me teary eyed. Knowing this beforehand, I'd have worried the atypical storytelling would be annoying, and the foot notes did have me a tad distracted at first, but I ended up finding all of it kind of brilliant. Furthermore, I found myself captivated by the way Leonard sees the world, how he perceives those around him. It's no doubt this kid is extremely intelligent. Maybe not in a straight-A book smart type, but in his analysis of people, of society. It's like he's already matured well beyond his years, but unfortunately this makes him an outcast. It's not hard to see why he doesn't blend in - It's not as if he wants to, either.<br><br>Throughout this story we get to understand how Leonard came to feel the way he does. He did not have the best, most happiest life, and a few happenings left him feeling confused and abandoned. It was all very saddening, making it impossible to not feel sympathy for this guy. He also felt so genuine, from the devalued way he sees himself, to his blunt, sometimes awkward interactions with others. Since he doesn't fit well with kids his own age, the side characters mostly consist of the adults in his life who are helping him fill the void he has had for so long. I loved his neighbour Walt with his chain smoking habit and amusing conversations in Bogart quotes. And I wish more teachers were like Herr Silverman; he's a true role model of human kindness in my eyes. <br><br>Event though they read pretty differently, this book reminded me of Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher. Maybe it's because it remains one of the few books on suicide that I've read - and that one touched me in a way like no other - but I'm certain those who enjoyed one will also love the other. It tugs at your emotions from the first page. Unlike Thirteen Reasons Why, though, you're not aware of how Leonard's story ends. On this note, I did wish the book's ending was a little longer, but I completely understand why it ended where it did.<br><br>It's gritty as gritty gets - it even makes you feel uncomfortable at times. Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock sends us into a the mind of a suicidal, atypical teenage boy that you're unlikely to ever forget!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9095726196378294041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1244256882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244256882" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1244256882?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244256882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1449832245809510497">I find this a very difficult book to review because on one hand, <u>it's subject matter is very important,</u> on the other, <b>I really didn't enjoy it very much.</b><br/><br/>There were times when I sympathized with the main character, Leonard Peacock. But an overwhelming amount of the time I found him <b>pretty unlikable.</b> And maybe that is how he's supposed to come off, I really don't know. It just made it difficult for me to understand him sometimes. <br/><br/>I felt similarly when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1217100.Thirteen_Reasons_Why' title='Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thirteen Reasons Why</a>, ultimately sad bu</span>
  <span id="freeText1449832245809510497" style="display:none">I find this a very difficult book to review because on one hand, <u>it's subject matter is very important,</u> on the other, <b>I really didn't enjoy it very much.</b><br /><br />There were times when I sympathized with the main character, Leonard Peacock. But an overwhelming amount of the time I found him <b>pretty unlikable.</b> And maybe that is how he's supposed to come off, I really don't know. It just made it difficult for me to understand him sometimes. <br /><br />I felt similarly when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1217100.Thirteen_Reasons_Why" title="Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher" rel="nofollow noopener">Thirteen Reasons Why</a>, ultimately sad but unconvinced. I am starting to think that perhaps books the deal intimately with suicide in this manner are not for me. I didn't look forward to reading it, and I'm relieved to be finished with it now.<br /><br />It's not that the book was awful, or written poorly, or any of those usual things that earn a lower rating from me. It's not that I wasn't able to grasp the ideas here, or feel pangs of empathy/compassion (because Leonard has been dealt a shitty hand in life). <br /><br /><b>I just don't think I was able to feel the emotions I was meant to feel deeply enough for a book like this to have a lasting impact.</b><br /><br />Also, I have a real problem with the structure of the physical copy of this book. All throughout the book there are these random footnotes, often times smack dab in the middle of a sentence. It made the reading experience very tedious, and <u>I honestly saw no reason the footnotes should be footnotes.</u> They would've fit fine into the paragraph as an extra sentence because it was a stream-of-consciousness writing style anyway?<br /><br />Then almost 3/4 of the way into the book we start seeing experimentation with words being scattered all over the page for dramatic effect, but there was no consistency &amp; it came off sort of forced.<br /><br />To top it all off, there are a couple letters written from the future to the main character placed between the chapters of the present storyline, and until the very end it's just hella confusing. I had no clue what I was supposed to gather from these letters, and <i>even now I feel no closure with the present story nor about the letters.</i><br /><br />The structure just made me feel like I was <b>jumping around everywhere.</b> My eyes were all over the page, I was in the present then in the future, my concentration was constantly interrupted.<br /><br />That's about as deep as I'll go into my problems with this one, because I truly believe this is a decent book that may speak volumes to other people. <b>It just largely wasn't my thing.</b></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_699013316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/699013316" />
    <a title="Mitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch"><img alt="Mitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396208595p2/8170554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/699013316?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mitch" href="/user/show/8170554-mitch">Mitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer699013316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1671728638592574252">Admittedly, I picked up <u>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</u> with a great deal of skepticism. I like my issues books hard-hitting, dark, and gritty, but I've not had much success finding many authors who can deliver the kind of bleak realism that for me is the holy grail of the genre. I want to say <u>Leonard Peacock</u> impressed me with its authenticity, but for a book billed as an unflinching examination, Matthew Quick flinched - multiple times.<br/><br/>What disappoints me most about <u>Leonard Peacock</u> is that it's writ</span>
  <span id="freeText1671728638592574252" style="display:none">Admittedly, I picked up <u>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</u> with a great deal of skepticism. I like my issues books hard-hitting, dark, and gritty, but I've not had much success finding many authors who can deliver the kind of bleak realism that for me is the holy grail of the genre. I want to say <u>Leonard Peacock</u> impressed me with its authenticity, but for a book billed as an unflinching examination, Matthew Quick flinched - multiple times.<br /><br />What disappoints me most about <u>Leonard Peacock</u> is that it's written from the perspective of a teenager about to kill his best friend, but in the frame of mind of an adult trying to understand and ultimately come to terms with the difficult path that drove him to that decision, and it didn't work for me. Frankly, I find it patronizing that the Leonard Peacock character is more an amalgam of stereotypes and excuses for explaining why a guy like him would be driven to do the unthinkable than a real character; I guess it makes people who struggle to understand the why feel better about themselves, but as a character study? - what I feel a book like this <i>should</i> be? - I'm sorry but it kind of sucks.<br /><br />Maybe my problem is that I felt a complete lack of empathy for Leonard Peacock. Quick paints his character in bold strokes that only fall apart when you think about it, and for me I really needed a more nuanced approach to connect with the character. A lot of the story is quite superficial, Leonard as expected is condescending, has a superiority complex (because obviously someone who decides to kill another person is going to look down on everyone), and rails against the establishment, to the point Quick's story feels very insincere, like he's writing this for adults based on his consultations with psychologists rather than for teens based on interactions with actual teenagers who have these problems - that's the only way I can explain how out of touch I feel Leonard's character is. Nor does Quick ever reconcile that angry at the world mass shooter stereotype with the guy who needs to give closure to the four people who mean something to him before he goes through with his plan - I mean, sometimes he's a psycho, sometimes he's a perfectly normal if depressing guy, and maybe he has multiple personalities or something but I never did get the sense that he was <i>one</i> character all the way through struggling with the childhood trauma Quick eventually reveals is the cause of his actions - it was just bold stroke, bold stroke, bold stroke, there just wasn't any nuance to fill in the gaps to his character.<br /><br />Instead, Quick goes for tired philosophical and nihilistic musings in the form of Leonard's attempted friendship with a home-schooled Christian girl to give his story the illusion of depth. You know, I expect a character who has suffered childhood trauma like Leonard has would feel a need to think about his place in the world, I'm not even going to call it a cliche, but this came off more like badgering people over their religious beliefs than any genuine soul-searching. And that's a problem throughout this entire book, for a story about a guy who takes one last shot at coming to terms with what happened to him before he ends it all, there just wasn't any genuine soul-searching, any depth, Quick tries to make Leonard sound deep with his writing style and the letters from the future and the distracting footnotes that are impossible to read in context with my ereader, but none of these things actually worked for me because each time I was pulled in one direction and started to get a feel for Leonard's character, Quick's overreliance on disaffected teen stereotypes just brought up too many inconsistencies and made the character impossible to connect with. Rather, it was all just a cheap after school special; I never felt Quick rises above trying to score points by feeding his readers the alienated lone gunman cliches we've come to associate with guys like Leonard to do an actual exploration of the character.<br /><br />I wanted to be impressed by Matthew Quick's hard-hitting, dark, and gritty storytelling, but <u>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</u> is none of these things. Sure I felt it was sad, but not sad as in emotional - sad as in pathetic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1671728638592574252" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/655294271?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=books-that-linger">books-that-linger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7584700-keertana?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655294271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14862728519892318702">I hardly know where to begin with <i>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock.</i> Suffice to say that this novel is brilliant, beautiful, and heart-breaking. It follows a teenage boy - Leonard Peacock - on his birthday as he chooses to kill another boy in his school and then commit suicide himself, all after giving the few special people in his life gifts to remember him by. As a foray into Quick's works, I can't say this was the happiest of reads, but it made my throat close up in grief and my knuckles fist into </span>
  <span id="freeText14862728519892318702" style="display:none">I hardly know where to begin with <i>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock.</i> Suffice to say that this novel is brilliant, beautiful, and heart-breaking. It follows a teenage boy - Leonard Peacock - on his birthday as he chooses to kill another boy in his school and then commit suicide himself, all after giving the few special people in his life gifts to remember him by. As a foray into Quick's works, I can't say this was the happiest of reads, but it made my throat close up in grief and my knuckles fist into my mouth to stop my sobs. It's difficult for me to articulate exactly <i>why</i> this book is so powerful, but Quick manages to capture the mindset of a lonely and hurting teenager perfectly. Moreover, the cast of secondary characters in this novel is stunning in their gray matter and unexpected depth. Leonard, especially, is a character our hearts go out to at once and I loved nothing more than his growth and the realistic, but hopeful, ending of this story. I truly believe this is one that everyone <i>must</i> read, if only to realize the pain that others carry within their hearts and learn to appreciate humanity a little bit more. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14862728519892318702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_681093136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681093136" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681093136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14994602072968929231">Woah. I'm just...woah. <b> This book kind of bopped me on the head and left my brain for dead. I love that. </b> It's an issue book, and while I don't think it adequately dealt with the issue, I think it presented the story realistically. <br/><br/>And then, you know, left us to stew in our own questions. WHY DID IT NOT ANSWER THE QUESTIONS? <br/><br/><b> It's narrated by, Leonard. </b> I don't want to give spoilers, but to put it bluntly: Leonard is considered "strange". He has a strange thought process. He likes strange things</span>
  <span id="freeText14994602072968929231" style="display:none">Woah. I'm just...woah. <b> This book kind of bopped me on the head and left my brain for dead. I love that. </b> It's an issue book, and while I don't think it adequately dealt with the issue, I think it presented the story realistically. <br /><br />And then, you know, left us to stew in our own questions. WHY DID IT NOT ANSWER THE QUESTIONS? <br /><br /><b> It's narrated by, Leonard. </b> I don't want to give spoilers, but to put it bluntly: Leonard is considered "strange". He has a strange thought process. He likes strange things (like old movies or listening to someone play violin every single day at school during lunch). He doesn't have friends. There are Reasons, but as if I'm going to tell you. Pfft. Read the book. What I loved about Leonard is I really felt like I was in his head during the book. I saw how he saw. It made me want to cry, because life's UNFAIR. Why does it need to be taht unfair?? Nothing that happened to Leonard was that "unusual" either, and that makes me sad. <br /><br />So Leonard is going to kill someone and then kill himself. (We know this from the blurb, too.) The book takes place over ONE DAY. I know, right?! ONE DAY. Leonard gives 4 presents to people he wants to thank...which is a sign of suicide, too, by the way (I know how to use google, too). It's interesting because we get to meet these 4 people. His neighbour. His favourite teacher. The violinist kid. The Jesus freak girl he couldn't have. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I'm really rather appalled at how the Iran friend treated Leonard. That was rude and cruel and mean. Just goes to show some people are really self-obsessed...Makes me sad.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><b> Sure! It's an issue book! But does it <i> deal </i>? </b> I don't really think so. ERMAGERD to that ending. Leave me alone to flail. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I will never forgive the mother for treating her son like that. Where was her brain? Couldn't she see? She didn't <i> want </i> to see.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It doesn't resolve, and I love it for that at the same time as hate it. Life doesn't resolve. But the book didn't exactly leave me feeling tremendously hopefully. Although, the messages....oh, gosh. The MESSAGES. There are some lines in there I could cry over. <b> People may suck, but there are ALWAYS people out there who will care. </b><br /><br />I feel so sad for Leonard. <br /><br /><b> I'm pretty sure this book will stay with me forever. SO JUST GO READ IT. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14994602072968929231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_698326560" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698326560" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/698326560?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer698326560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8967947441678231760"><i>“I'm trying to let him know what I'm about to do.<br/>I'm hoping he can save me, even though I realize he can't.” </i><br/><br/><b>REACTION AFTER READING THE BOOK</b><br/><br/>I didn't really know what I felt after reading this book.<br/><s>Sorrow. Pain. Hurt. Disappointment.Anger.Loneliness.</s><br/>This book gave me a lot more to think about.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380433554ra/872530.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Forgive me, Leonard Peacock</b> is one of those books that I think is a must read for everyone.<br/>Don't be mislead by the title.<br/>This book is not in any way comical.<br/>It is not in any way plain humorous.<br/>It is just not</span>
  <span id="freeText8967947441678231760" style="display:none"><i>“I'm trying to let him know what I'm about to do.<br>I'm hoping he can save me, even though I realize he can't.” </i><br><br><b>REACTION AFTER READING THE BOOK</b><br><br>I didn't really know what I felt after reading this book.<br><s>Sorrow. Pain. Hurt. Disappointment.Anger.Loneliness.</s><br>This book gave me a lot more to think about.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380433554ra/872530.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Forgive me, Leonard Peacock</b> is one of those books that I think is a must read for everyone.<br>Don't be mislead by the title.<br>This book is not in any way comical.<br>It is not in any way plain humorous.<br>It is just not.<br>There were some witty lines that at regular instances would make me smile or laugh at times but it didn't do that to me on this one.<br>The story was just tad to serious.<br>This book was sad. But in a way, it was very beautiful.<br><br>Here's the short <b>GIST</b><br><br>Leonard Peacock has a plan.<br>Today was his birthday but instead of receiving gifts, he was planning to give 4 people a gift instead.<br>These four people were the ones who touched his life the most.<br>These four people were the only ones he thought bothered with him.<br>But that wasn't the only thing he had planned for his birthday.<br>As a grand finale, he was going to kill himself.<br>But before that, he was going to kill his former best friend with his grandfather's P-38 pistol.<br><br><b>FIRST IMPRESSIONS</b><br><br>The title got me fooled. I thought at first it was going to be an easy read.<br>Before I got the book, I checked the synopsis here at Goodreads first.<br>It sounded serious but still, I wasn't expecting the contents to be what it was.<br><br><b>MEET THE CHARACTERS</b><br><br><b>Leonard</b><br><br>I feel for Leonard. I have to admit though that he wasn't a very easy character to love. He was bitter. He was sarcastic. At times he thinks he is better than everyone else. Who would love a character like that? He was more of an antihero in every aspect. Although this book reminded me of Perks of Being a Wallflower, Leonard was in no way like Charlie. Leonard thinks very much different from people his age and I think that's what sets him apart. His views on life after teenage years and what adulthood is very mature. Aside from all this, Leonard suffered from some traumatic stuff in his past that he cannot tell anyone. Just like Charlie (from Perks of Being a Wallflower). The only difference is Leonard was aware of it happening. He was aware but too scared to do anything as he wanted to belong. He didn't want to be alone. I guess that's really where everything started. But that's not the only thing I guess. Partly, I think his mom would have the biggest fault in all this. I'm sorry. I just had to say it. If she wasn't so conveniently inattentive I don't think Leonard would be in the situation that he was then. <br><br><b>Herr Silverman</b><br><br>He would have to be my favorite character in this book. He was Leonard's Hollocaust teacher. He knew from the moment Leonard gave him his gift that something was wrong. How did he know? Because he was paying attention to him. Unlike his mom. Unlike his other teachers. Unlike his classmates. He knew something was up. I think he already knew when he bumped that question in class. I wasn't expecting the secret he was keeping. I was thinking of something else entirely. I was thinking that he was previously suicidal or something but he wasn't. It was very different from that. Everyone needs a Herr Silveman in life. Someone who would be there to listen and observe and help. <br><br><b>Asher</b><br><br>I seriously want to blow this <s>mthrf*cking</s> guys head off! It's not until towards the end of this book that you find out why Leonard hates him so much. If you find out, I'm sure you'd want to beat the daylights out of this kid too! He used to be a really good kid. But I gues some people do change. Why? Also because of the people who surrounds them. <br><br><b>Linda</b><br><br>I really hate her. Every time she opens her mouth all I could feel was anger and hatred towards this woman. Who is she? He's Leonards <s>good-for-nothing</s> Mom. Leonard's still a kid. Although he could think way beyond his years, he still needs someone who will give him caring and affection. But where is this woman? Oh somewhere. Having fun with her French boyfriend. But does she ever checks on poor Leonard. Nah. Not at all.<br><br><b>HIGHLIGHTS</b><br><br>- i liked how on the first chapter you'll already know what the character is going to do. and then you gradually find out what happened before and you'll also know what's currently happening. the story telling was fluid and easy to read despite the sensitive topic.<br><br>- Herr Silverman was a highlight for me.<br><br>- the chronological arrangement of the story was good.<br><br>- Leonard's letter to the future was good. I'd probably do it at some point.<br><br>- the truth in Quick's writing is something that I really couldn't get enough of.<br><br><b>FINAL WORDS</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380433554ra/872531.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This wouldn't really solve anything.<br>Killing yourself is just like accepting defeat.<br><br><b>First they ignore you, then<br>they laugh at you, they they<br>fight you, then you win.</b><br><br>Everyone experience problems. Leonard isn't the only one with problems. I'm not saying that his problem is worse than others because I think there are other people with much more issues to handle. <br>But some are able to cope with it. <br>No matter how hard the situation is. No matter how hopeless they seem to be.<br>Why? <br>I think its because of the support they get from the people around them.<br>If there were more people around Leonard who would care for him, do you think he'll still feel the same way?<br>Do you think he will still consider suicide?<br>No he wouldn't.<br>Why? <br>Because he feels that he has someone. He has someone to lean on when times get hard. He has someone to talk to when his mom disregards him or when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Asher was doing the things he was doing to Leonard. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I think people still fail to understand how our action can greatly affect other people.<br>I think its important that we know the value of what we do or what we say.<br>Of course we may not always do and say the right things but at least we should be cautious.<br>We wouldn't know if we are saying the wrong words to a suicidal person.<br>One wrong word or action may cause that person to end it all.<br><br>In my review of Perks of Being a Wallflower, I mentioned that things could change based on the decisions and choices that we could make.<br>Things will remain the same if you don't do anything about it<br>I think that somehow Leonard was also to blame for what was happening to him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380433554ra/872532.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He doesn't believe that his future would be better so that's what caused him to want to end it all.<br>His choice was to keep silent and that choice led him what was happening to him in the present.<br>If he had done differently, I think things would have been different too.<br>Every action has its own consequences and I think this book also highlighted that.<br>We can't always blame other people, at some point we ourselves are also to blame.<br><br>I would just like to end my review with a quote as I feel that this is one truth I have learned when I was reading this. Herr Silverman was the one who said it in this book:<br><br><i>“There's a lot for you to live for. Good things are definitely in your future, Leonard. I'm sure of it. You have no idea how many interesting people you'll meet after high school's over. Your life partner, your best friend, the most wonderful person you'll ever know is sitting in some high school right now waiting to graduate and walk into your life - maybe even feeling all the same things you are, maybe even wondering about you, hoping that you're strong enough to make it to the future where you'll meet.” </i><br><br>I rate this:<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/star%20gif/SAKORY/Gifs/1296064yv2vt9d05a.gif?o=33" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380416409ra/822333.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1609459952" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609459952" />
    <a title="k " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41536721-k"><img alt="k " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605702001p2/41536721.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609459952?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="k " class="user" itemprop="url" name="k " href="/user/show/41536721-k">k </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609459952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6022764202583792396">This book is mainly about a suicidal and homicidal eighteen-year-old Leonard Peacock. <br/><br/>1.) plot - the fact that I just finished this book in literally just one night just proves how this book was beautifully written. That this novel was tragic yet eye-opening. <br/><br/>Pacing of the book was truly incredible, I love how the author add a bit of humor to this novel when in fact, the issue this book tackled was really serious. <br/><br/>And you may call me hypocrite or what but this book made me realize MORE that you </span>
  <span id="freeText6022764202583792396" style="display:none">This book is mainly about a suicidal and homicidal eighteen-year-old Leonard Peacock. <br /><br />1.) plot - the fact that I just finished this book in literally just one night just proves how this book was beautifully written. That this novel was tragic yet eye-opening. <br /><br />Pacing of the book was truly incredible, I love how the author add a bit of humor to this novel when in fact, the issue this book tackled was really serious. <br /><br />And you may call me hypocrite or what but this book made me realize MORE that you SHOULD be kind to everyone for everyone is fighting a battle. Anyways, what I just said is totally not mine, I think I saw this quote in Facebook. So, please spare my sin. <br /><br />And for me, as simple as it is, I seriously do wholeheartedly agree with it. And that perhaps all people really need in life is security and comfort, love in general. <br /><br />2.) writing style - blimey, the writing style was absolutely fantastic. Like I mentioned, the topic was pretty solemn yet the author mixed a bit of humor in it. <br /><br />The narrator felt like this friend to me. And God knows how much I wanted to give Leonard a massive warm hug, simply because he needed it and also because I wanted to. <br /><br />Crying in the middle of the night was probably can be considered as creepy and depressing at the same time but tell you what, I practically don't care. What happened to Leonard was truly heart wrecking. I really did cried while reading the climax and the ending. <br /><br />And that leads us to a topic regarding to the ending. Well, it's an open-ending! I don't know whether Leonard will go to this new path or will just choose this old path. Believe me, I don't wanna spoil the hell out of you guys. <br /><br />Regardless of that, I was somehow disappointed at the ending for I am expecting what EXACTLY happened to our dear Leonard Peacock. <br /><br /><br />3.) Characters - <br />Leonard - first of all, the fact that he was a fan of literature and old movies were enough to love him. Leonard was just this typical hormonal slash lonely boy, seeking for the love of his mother and perhaps somehow in the midst of not wanting to earn her affection anymore. That he was a victim, of his mother, his ex-bestfriend and the society. <br /><br />Herr Silverman - was one great man. Reading WW2 facts is seriously my thing so that's a plus. I love that he was there when Leonard needed him even though he has the right to just ignore him because first of all, it's not part of his job and that he's not gaining any profit here. But regardless of that, he still chose to be an heroic teacher. <br /><br />Walt - definitely my favorite character in the novel. He stood as a father to Leonard. He was the one who influenced Leonard to give black-and-white movies a try. I love him. I love how he freaked out when he knew something's wrong with Leonard. <br /><br />Asher - Perhaps it's my nature to see good things in every person because I believe that our deAr Asher here was also a victim. <br /><br />SPOILER ALERT!<br /><br />Sure, he committed this horrible thing to Leonard but didn't you realized what exactly happened when Asher went fishing with his uncle. That, perhaps he too, had also fooled Asher that they're going to "have some fun and feel good" <br /><br />I feel so fucked-up about that one, you know considering that when Leonard first caught a glimpse of this certain uncle, he thought he was cool and kind! <br /><br />I mean, imagine how terrifying that may be for Asher! Being "raped" by his UNCLE WHO PLAYED AS A NICE GUY THE WHOLE TIME!! MAN!! This world is seriously fucked up. And I feel bad for both boys! This inhuman uncle really did ruined the friendship between Leonard and Asher!! <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3200912302?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L A i N E Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L A i N E Y" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y">L A i N E Y</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3200912302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3007052885386994184">I don’t want this to come out wrong by any means because school shooting is one of the most civilized evil in modern times. But I feel this book was too gimmicky somehow. Like intentionally misleading as to present itself to be sensational when it isn’t, not really. If the author would just write about Leonard’s life and what he had to endure in the past and what his life still is till the present, which includes putting up with his really shitty ‘mom’, I would have totally been all in for that.</span>
  <span id="freeText3007052885386994184" style="display:none">I don’t want this to come out wrong by any means because school shooting is one of the most civilized evil in modern times. But I feel this book was too gimmicky somehow. Like intentionally misleading as to present itself to be sensational when it isn’t, not really. If the author would just write about Leonard’s life and what he had to endure in the past and what his life still is till the present, which includes putting up with his really shitty ‘mom’, I would have totally been all in for that. Leonard has it terrible already and I’d root for him all the way. But the book wouldn’t be as “sensational” right? No. So let’s add the facade of “He brings his (Nazi) gun to school” tagline and now everyone is at attention for it, jackpot! Instant buzz amiright? URG. <br /><br />I don’t know that’s just how I feel after finishing this.<br /><br /><br />The audiobook featured a very good performance by Noah Galvin though so that’s something, I guess.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3007052885386994184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/577831658?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=ya-for-grown-ups">ya-for-grown-ups</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer577831658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5151599900479015900">This is the story of one day in Leonard Peacock’s life. The most important day he’ll ever live. Not only is it his 18th birthday, it’s also the day where he will kill Asher Beal and then himself. Follow Leonard through this most remarkable day as he says his farewells to the four most important people in his life – on the last day of his own.<br/><br/>Characters like Leonard Peacock (i.e., Holden Caulfield, Gene from A Separate Peace, Charlie from The Perks of Being a Wallflower, Lucky Linderman from Ever</span>
  <span id="freeText5151599900479015900" style="display:none">This is the story of one day in Leonard Peacock’s life. The most important day he’ll ever live. Not only is it his 18th birthday, it’s also the day where he will kill Asher Beal and then himself. Follow Leonard through this most remarkable day as he says his farewells to the four most important people in his life – on the last day of his own.<br><br>Characters like Leonard Peacock (i.e., Holden Caulfield, Gene from A Separate Peace, Charlie from The Perks of Being a Wallflower, Lucky Linderman from Everybody Sees the Ants, etc., etc.) can sometimes seem to be a dime a dozen. They are generally fairly similar in that they have a case of arrested development and have one defining experience that made them who they are (that is easily foretold 200 pages in advance). I’ll admit that it took me awhile to really sink into this book because I thought it was just going to be a knock-off of one of the aforementioned. Although there were similarities, Matthew Quick’s writing set Leonard apart from some of the others. Quick really GETS how to write a character dealing with mental illness (Pat in The Silver Linings Playbook – I mean GENIUS!). Leonard’s pain comes through every page once he REALLY starts letting you in to his life. <br><br>Forewarning: Not to insult the youngsters out there since this is a YA book, but it is a YA book for EXTREMELY mature youth. This sucker deals with über depressing, dark and heavy subject matter. It will make you cry the “ugly cry”, but also leaves a message of:<br><br><a href="http://s1364.photobucket.com/user/doublely/media/love_zpsff297463.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415822i/821048._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo love_zpsff297463.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1424845274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424845274" />
    <a title="Maria (Big City Bookworm)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm"><img alt="Maria (Big City Bookworm)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558875339p2/2567068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424845274?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria (Big City Bookworm)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria (Big City Bookworm)" href="/user/show/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm">Maria (Big City Bookworm)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2567068-maria-big-city-bookworm?shelf=on-my-shelf">on-my-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424845274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5698058953795952791"><a href='https://bigcitybookworm.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455899354i/18166743.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/><b><i>“we can simultaneously be human and monster—that both of those possibilities are in all of us.”</i></b><br/><br/>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock is one of those books that just took me by complete surprise. I didn’t do a lot of research before picking it up and I definitely hadn’t seen many people talk about it. I found it on sale and I decided to pick it up on a whim. I’m really glad that I did.<br/><br/>--<br/><br/><b>What I Liked</b><br/><br/><b>The discussion of important social issues.</b> I feel like I’ve been reading a lot of books recently that contain</span>
  <span id="freeText5698058953795952791" style="display:none"><a href="https://bigcitybookworm.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455899354i/18166743.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br><b><i>“we can simultaneously be human and monster—that both of those possibilities are in all of us.”</i></b><br><br>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock is one of those books that just took me by complete surprise. I didn’t do a lot of research before picking it up and I definitely hadn’t seen many people talk about it. I found it on sale and I decided to pick it up on a whim. I’m really glad that I did.<br><br>--<br><br><b>What I Liked</b><br><br><b>The discussion of important social issues.</b> I feel like I’ve been reading a lot of books recently that contain characters who are dealing with certain social or mental issues. I’m really glad to have been lucky enough to find multiple books that deal with these issues as I personally believe that they are extremely important. When I picked up Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock, I figured that it might deal with some sort of mental illness as the synposis clearly mentions that Leonard is planning to kill a classmate and then himself. What I didn’t expect was for it to dive so deep into the reasoning behind his reasoning. I’ve read a few books now that deal with school shootings, and while they explore the perspectives of the students that are trapped throughout the school, they hardly ever tell to story from the perspective of the shooter. I am in no way implying that having the shooters reasoning justifies their actions, but I do like the idea of knowing why they are acting the way that they are. I love that this book explained Leonard’s life and issues in detail. Again, this doesn’t justify his desire to kill his classmate and then himself, but it does provide an insight into why Leonard is feeling this dark and hopeless.<br><br><b>The characters, major &amp; minor.</b> A lot of the characters throughout this book are problematic in their own way. I liked reading from Leonard’s perspective. I enjoyed learning about his lack of friends, his troubling past and his terrible home-life. I know that saying I enjoyed reading about these things might not be the best way to describe it, but it really added depth to his character. I liked reading about his relationship with his neighbour Walt and his Holocaust professor, Herr Silverman. All of Leonard’s interactions with these other characters helped to add more to his story.<br><br><b>The writing style.</b> Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock was extremely fast paced and I could not stop reading. Matthew Quick did an exceptional job in writing the voice of Leonard. He is definitely a memorable character with an even more memorable story.<br><br>--<br><br><b>What I Didn’t Like</b><br><br><b>The scenes with Lauren.</b> I really don’t know why, but I just couldn’t stand any of the scenes with her. I know that these moments were important as Leonard thought that maybe finding faith in God might help him and his issues. I get why these scenes were included, but I just couldn’t stand Lauren. The interactions between her and Leonard were just a little awkward for me…<br><br><b>This book really surprised me.</b> I didn’t really know what to expect going into it and it ended up surprising me in the best way possible. I look forward to reading more from Matthew Quick in the future!<br><br>--<br><br><b>Initial post reading thoughts:</b><br><br>I'm actually surprised about how much I enjoyed this. Not because I had heard bad things, but mostly because I hadn't really heard much about it at all! I got it really cheap as an audiobook when audible was having a sale and I'm so glad that I took a chance and purchased it. I wasn't expecting it to be as dark as it was. I also really enjoyed the idea of learning about what drives someone to want to kill someone/themselves. With all these books about school shooting especially, we rarely learn about the shooter's motives. Not that their motives justify their actions in any way, don't get me wrong, but I do like the idea of knowing why they're doing what they're doing. Yeah...I really liked this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5698058953795952791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2405553599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2405553599" />
    <a title="Gray Cox" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63603460-gray-cox"><img alt="Gray Cox" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565355708p2/63603460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2405553599?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gray Cox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gray Cox" href="/user/show/63603460-gray-cox">Gray Cox</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63603460-gray-cox?shelf=wheres-the-tissues">wheres-the-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63603460-gray-cox?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63603460-gray-cox?shelf=made-me-think">made-me-think</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63603460-gray-cox?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63603460-gray-cox?shelf=mental-illness-rep">mental-illness-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63603460-gray-cox?shelf=morally-conflicted">morally-conflicted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2405553599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2020674157398324137"><i>"I'm going to kill you later today," I say to the guy in the mirror, he just smiles back at me like he can't wait. <br/>"Promise?" I hear someone say, which freaks me out, because my lips didn't move.<br/>I mean-it wasn't me who said, "Promise?"<br/>It's like there's a voice trapped inside the glass. So I stop looking in the mirror. Just for good measure, I smash that mirror with a coffee mug, because I don't want that mirror to speak to me ever again.-(pg. 15)</i><br/><br/><b>When I saw what this book was about I was worried.</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2020674157398324137" style="display:none"><i>"I'm going to kill you later today," I say to the guy in the mirror, he just smiles back at me like he can't wait. <br />"Promise?" I hear someone say, which freaks me out, because my lips didn't move.<br />I mean-it wasn't me who said, "Promise?"<br />It's like there's a voice trapped inside the glass. So I stop looking in the mirror. Just for good measure, I smash that mirror with a coffee mug, because I don't want that mirror to speak to me ever again.-(pg. 15)</i><br /><br /><b>When I saw what this book was about I was worried.</b><br /><br />Too often suicide and mental illness is presented as easy and a way to get revenge, too often books about the subject fail to capture how lost a person is and how horrible it is to feel this way. <br /><br /><b>Not this book.</b><br /><br />This book is the gritty, ugly, horrifying truth. <br /><br />Leonard is suffering with trauma and depression, his past is full of neglect and abuse, so one day he decides he wants to end it all as well as take his revenge.<br /><br />The book follows him as he plans to kill his former best friend, and as he says goodbye to the three only people he ever cared about. <br /><br /><b>This book hit me so hard.</b> There are so many teens like Leonard, and even Asher.<br /><br /><i>But really-why do some people post the correct ways to commit suicide on the Internet? Do they want weird, sad people like me to go away permanently?-(pg. 7)</i><br /><br /><b>This book starts off with no hope and ends with so much hope, it's so amazing and beautiful, and every teenager suffering with thoughts like this needs to read this book.</b><br /><br /><i>Forgive Me, Leonard Peacock</i> brings something back to the young adult world that has been missing: empathy, understanding, and hope. <br /><br /><i>"My life will get better? You really believe that?" I ask.<br />"It can. If you're willing to work."<br />"What work?"<br />"Not letting the world destroy you. That's a daily battle."-(pg. 227)</i><br /><br /><b>Content warnings:</b> <br /><br />-Tons of swearing and crude jokes.<br /><br />-Characters suffer from sexual abuse in the past. <br /><br />-Mental illness/ depressing thoughts.<br /><br /><b>In the end, this book is so important.</b> If you are struggling with suicidal thoughts, please know that you are not alone, and that things will get better. There is hope. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="2020674157398324137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823083866?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823083866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer524470078829785282"><b>2 stars<br/>Full review to come</b><br/><br/>A few things about my reading experience ...<br/><br/>I totally thought this book was going to be a cute contemporary because this is what happens when you like to read books without knowing a single thing about the book before you start.<br/><br/>This is NOT a cute contemporary, but it is a very deep dark and important topic.<br/><br/>I have zero interest in this book but like ... I want to.<br/><br/>It's not the topic that has curved my interest into disinterest ... I just don't care about the story or the </span>
  <span id="freeText524470078829785282" style="display:none"><b>2 stars<br />Full review to come</b><br /><br />A few things about my reading experience ...<br /><br />I totally thought this book was going to be a cute contemporary because this is what happens when you like to read books without knowing a single thing about the book before you start.<br /><br />This is NOT a cute contemporary, but it is a very deep dark and important topic.<br /><br />I have zero interest in this book but like ... I want to.<br /><br />It's not the topic that has curved my interest into disinterest ... I just don't care about the story or the characters. Maybe I just wasn't in the mood ... I don't know. <br />Something.<br /><br />*shrugs*<br /><br />I was finally able to drift into mild interest toward the end so there's that. The writing was decent and the topic was important and the story was decent and I had no connection to any of it at all. <br /><br />Just a meh read overall.</span>
  <a data-text-id="524470078829785282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Vs08QnK7TXDTnVLcfNz2S26WjH1Tu8y98ygke0yv2zKELFW/anJP8/CHOZz2ZWsJs+ZT17H9IGbBOGk1xuhwEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7Z06+qXSMVZA6POBTs/OBYbbgRqHctOGzrFwyUJAozc/fFMHvRsz1WPymMHEdlNHW6tesGU0P138oT2HyAcIFQ==')})
  }

//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_18460392'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392-all-the-bright-places?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">All the Bright Places<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/45592.Jennifer_Niven?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Jennifer Niven<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.15 avg rating &mdash; 305,035 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2015\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer222983748174750797\">The Fault in Our Stars meets Eleanor and Park in this exhilarating and heart-wrenching love story about a girl who learns to live from a boy who intends to die.Soon to be a major motion picture starring Elle Fanning! Theodore Finch is fascinated by d<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText222983748174750797\" style=\"display:none\">The Fault in Our Stars meets Eleanor and Park in this exhilarating and heart-wrenching love story about a girl who learns to live from a boy who intends to die.Soon to be a major motion picture starring Elle Fanning! Theodore Finch is fascinated by death, and he constantly thinks of ways he might kill himself. But each time, something good, no matter how small, stops him. Violet Markey lives for the future, counting the days until graduation, when she can escape her Indiana town and her aching grief in the wake of her sister’s recent death. When Finch and Violet meet on the ledge of the bell tower at school, it’s unclear who saves whom. And when they pair up on a project to discover the “natural wonders” of their state, both Finch and Violet make more important discoveries: It’s only with Violet that Finch can be himself—a weird, funny, live-out-loud guy who’s not such a freak after all. And it’s only with Finch that Violet can forget to count away the days and start living them. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10108269626355617085">Matthew Quick is the New York Times bestselling author of THE SILVER LININGS PLAYBOOK, which was made into an Oscar-winning film; THE GOOD LUCK OF RIGHT NOW; LOVE MAY FAIL; THE REASON YOU’RE ALIVE; and four young adult novels: SORTA LIKE A ROCK STAR; BOY21; FORGIVE ME, LEONARD PEACOCK; and EVERY EXQUISITE THING. His work has been translated into more than thirty languages, received a PEN/Hemingway</span>
  <span id="freeText10108269626355617085" style="display:none">Matthew Quick is the New York Times bestselling author of THE SILVER LININGS PLAYBOOK, which was made into an Oscar-winning film; THE GOOD LUCK OF RIGHT NOW; LOVE MAY FAIL; THE REASON YOU’RE ALIVE; and four young adult novels: SORTA LIKE A ROCK STAR; BOY21; FORGIVE ME, LEONARD PEACOCK; and EVERY EXQUISITE THING. His work has been translated into more than thirty languages, received a PEN/Hemingway Award Honorable Mention, was an LA Times Book Prize finalist, a New York Times Book Review Editors’ Choice, a #1 bestseller in Brazil, a Deutscher Jugendliteratur Preis 2016 (German Youth Literature Prize) nominee, and selected by Nancy Pearl as one of Summer’s Best Books for NPR. The Hollywood Reporter has named him one of Hollywood’s 25 Most Powerful Authors. All of his books have been optioned for film.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10108269626355617085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
